<p>The <b>Jagiellonian dynasty</b> was a royal <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">dynasty</a>, founded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jogaila" title="Jogaila">Jogaila</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duke of Lithuania">Grand Duke of Lithuania</a>, who in 1386 was baptized as Władysław, married Queen (strictly King)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jadwiga_of_Poland" title="Jadwiga of Poland">Jadwiga of Poland</a>, and was crowned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_Poland" title="King of Poland">King of Poland</a> as Władysław II Jagiełło. The dynasty reigned in several <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central European</a> countries between the 14th and 16th centuries. Members of the dynasty were <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_(1385%E2%80%931569)" title="Kingdom of Poland (1385–1569)">Kings</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Poland_(1385%E2%80%931569)" title="History of Poland (1385–1569)">Poland</a> (1386–1572), Grand Dukes of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Lithuania</a> (1377–1392 and 1440–1572), Kings of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Hungary</a> (1440–1444 and 1490–1526), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kings_of_Bohemia" title="Kings of Bohemia">Kings</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a> (1471–1526).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> between the Kingdom of Poland and the Grand Duchy of Lithuania (converted in 1569 with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lublin" title="Treaty of Lublin">Treaty of Lublin</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>) is the reason for the common appellation "<a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_union" title="Polish–Lithuanian union">Poland–Lithuania</a>" in discussions about the area from the <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">Late Middle Ages</a> onward. One Jagiellonian briefly ruled both Poland and Hungary (1440–44), and two others ruled both <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> (1490–1526) and then continued in the <a href="/wiki/Distaff" title="Distaff">distaff</a> line as a branch of the House of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Polish_Golden_Age" title="Polish Golden Age">Polish "Golden Age</a>", the period of the reigns of <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_I_the_Old" title="Sigismund I the Old">Sigismund I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_II_Augustus" title="Sigismund II Augustus">Sigismund II</a>, the last two Jagiellonian kings, or more generally the 16th century, is most often identified with the rise of the culture of <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland" title="Renaissance in Poland">Polish Renaissance</a>. The cultural flowering had its material base in the prosperity of the elites, both the landed nobility and urban patriciate at such centers as <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Cracow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gdańsk">Danzig</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jagiellonian.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1764" data-file-width="1752" height="262" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Jagiellonian.png/260px-Jagiellonian.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Jagiellonian.png/390px-Jagiellonian.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Jagiellonian.png/520px-Jagiellonian.png 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jagiellonian.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
At the end of the 15th century, the Jagiellonians reigned over vast territories stretching from the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Sea" title="Adriatic Sea">Adriatic Sea</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name comes from Jogaila (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jagie%C5%82%C5%82o" title="Jagiełło">Jagiełło</a>), the first Grand Duke of Lithuania to become King of Poland. In Polish, the dynasty is known as <i>Jagiellonowie</i> and the patronymic form: <i>Jagiellończyk</i>; in <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a> it is called <i>Jogailaičiai</i>, in <a href="/wiki/Belarusian_language" title="Belarusian language">Belarusian</a> <i>Яґайлавічы</i> (<i>Jagajłavičy</i>), in <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a> <i>Jagelló</i>, and in <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a> <i>Jagellonci</i>, as well as <i>Jagello</i> or <i>Jagellon</i> in Latin.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-dynasty_background">Pre-dynasty background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-dynasty background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The rule of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piast" title="Piast">Piasts</a>, the earlier Polish ruling house (c. 962–1370) had ended with the death of King <a href="/wiki/Casimir_III_the_Great" title="Casimir III the Great">Casimir III the Great</a>. <a href="/wiki/Gediminids" title="Gediminids">Gediminids</a>, the immediate predecessors of the first Jagiellonian, were rulers of medieval <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> with the title of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Duke" title="Grand Duke">Grand Duke</a></i>. Their realm, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>, was chiefly inhabited by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithuanian_people" title="Lithuanian people">Lithuanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruthenians" title="Ruthenians">Ruthenians</a>.</p>
<p>Jogaila, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eponymous" title="Eponymous">eponymous</a> first ruler of the Jagiellonin dynasty, started as the Grand Duke of Lithuania. As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Krewo" title="Union of Krewo">Union of Krewo</a> he then converted to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> and married the 11-year-old <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hedwig_of_Poland" title="Hedwig of Poland">Hedwig of Poland</a> (Jadwiga in Polish) (daughter of King <a href="/wiki/Louis_I_of_Hungary" title="Louis I of Hungary">Louis I of Hungary</a> from the Angevins Dynasty). Thereby he became <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_Poland" title="King of Poland">King of Poland</a> and founded the dynasty. <a href="/wiki/Capetian_House_of_Anjou" title="Capetian House of Anjou">Angevin</a> rulers were the second and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jagiellonian" title="Jagiellonian">Jagiellonian</a> third dynasty of Polish Kings.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Poland">Kingdom of Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jogaila_and_W.C5.82adys.C5.82aw_III">Jogaila and Władysław III</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Jogaila and Władysław III">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Polish.E2.80.93Lithuanian_union">Polish–Lithuanian union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Polish–Lithuanian union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jagiello-portret-1790.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2376" data-file-width="1899" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Jagiello-portret-1790.jpg/220px-Jagiello-portret-1790.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Jagiello-portret-1790.jpg/330px-Jagiello-portret-1790.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Jagiello-portret-1790.jpg/440px-Jagiello-portret-1790.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jagiello-portret-1790.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<b><a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_II_Jagie%C5%82%C5%82o" title="Władysław II Jagiełło">Jogaila</a></b>, later <b>Władysław II Jagiełło</b> (c. 1352/1362 – 1 June 1434) was <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duke of Lithuania</a> (1377–1434), <a href="/wiki/List_of_Polish_monarchs" title="List of Polish monarchs">King of Poland</a> (1386–1399) alongside his wife <a href="/wiki/Jadwiga_of_Poland" title="Jadwiga of Poland">Jadwiga</a>, and then sole King of Poland.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1385 the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Krewo" title="Union of Krewo">Union of Krewo</a> was signed between <a href="/wiki/Jadwiga_of_Poland" title="Jadwiga of Poland">Queen Jadwiga of Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_II_Jagie%C5%82%C5%82o" title="Władysław II Jagiełło">Jogaila</a>, the Grand Duke of Lithuania, the last <a href="/wiki/Paganism" title="Paganism">pagan</a> state in Europe. The act arranged for Jogaila's <a href="/wiki/Christianization_of_Lithuania" title="Christianization of Lithuania">baptism</a> (after which Jogaila was known in Poland by his baptismal name, Władysław, and the Polish version of his Lithuanian name, Jagiełło) (Zamoyski, the Polish Way) and for the couple's marriage and constituted the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_union" title="Polish–Lithuanian union">Polish–Lithuanian union</a>. The Union strengthened both nations in their shared opposition to the <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_Order" title="Teutonic Order">Teutonic Knights</a> and the growing threat of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Grand Duchy of Moscow</a>. Uniquely in Europe, the union connected two states geographically located on the opposite sides of the great civilizational divide between the <a href="/wiki/Western_Christianity" title="Western Christianity">Western</a> or Latin, and the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern</a> or Byzantine worlds.<sup>[5]</sup></p>
<p>The intention of the Union was to create a common state under Władysław II Jagiełło, but the Polish ruling oligarchy's idea of incorporation of Lithuania into Poland turned out to be unrealistic. There would be territorial disputes and warfare between Poland and Lithuania or Lithuanian factions; the Lithuanians at times had even found it expedient to conspire with the Teutonic Knights against the <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>. Geographic consequences of the dynastic union and the preferences of the Jagiellonian kings accelerated the process of reorientation of Polish territorial priorities to the east.<sup>[3]</sup> The political influence of the Jagiellonian kings was diminishing during this period, which was accompanied by the ever increasing role in central government and national affairs of landed nobility.<sup>[a]</sup> The royal dynasty, however, had a stabilizing effect on Poland's politics. The <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poland_during_the_Jagiellonian_dynasty" title="History of Poland during the Jagiellonian dynasty">Jagiellonian Era</a> is often regarded as a period of maximum political power, great prosperity, and in its later stage, <a href="/wiki/Polish_Golden_Age" title="Polish Golden Age">the Golden Age of Polish culture</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Struggle_with_the_Teutonic_Knights">Struggle with the Teutonic Knights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Struggle with the Teutonic Knights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Matejko_Baptism_of_Ladislaus_of_Varna.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="518" data-file-width="761" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Matejko_Baptism_of_Ladislaus_of_Varna.jpg/220px-Matejko_Baptism_of_Ladislaus_of_Varna.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Matejko_Baptism_of_Ladislaus_of_Varna.jpg/330px-Matejko_Baptism_of_Ladislaus_of_Varna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Matejko_Baptism_of_Ladislaus_of_Varna.jpg/440px-Matejko_Baptism_of_Ladislaus_of_Varna.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Matejko_Baptism_of_Ladislaus_of_Varna.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Baptism of <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_III_of_Poland" title="Władysław III of Poland">Władysław III of Poland</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian%E2%80%93Teutonic_War" title="Polish–Lithuanian–Teutonic War">The Great War</a> of 1409–1411, precipitated by the Lithuanian uprising in the Order controlled <a href="/wiki/Samogitia" title="Samogitia">Samogitia</a>, included the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grunwald" title="Battle of Grunwald">Battle of Grunwald</a> (Tannenberg), where the Polish and Lithuanian-Rus' armies completely defeated the <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_Order" title="Teutonic Order">Teutonic Knights</a>. The offensive that followed lost its impact with the ineffective siege of <a href="/wiki/Malbork" title="Malbork">Malbork</a> (Marienburg). The failure to take the fortress and eliminate the Teutonic (later Prussian) state had for Poland dire historic consequences in the 18th, 19th and 20th centuries. <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Thorn_(1411)" title="Peace of Thorn (1411)">The Peace of Thorn</a> (1411) had given Poland and Lithuania rather modest territorial adjustments, including Samogitia. Afterwards there were negotiations and peace deals that didn't hold, more military campaigns and arbitrations. One attempted, unresolved arbitration took place at the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Constance" title="Council of Constance">Council of Constance</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Polish.E2.80.93Hungarian_union">Polish–Hungarian union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Polish–Hungarian union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Hussite_Wars" title="Hussite Wars">Hussite Wars</a> (1420–1434), Jagiełło, <a href="/wiki/Vytautas" title="Vytautas">Vytautas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_Korybut" title="Sigismund Korybut">Sigismund Korybut</a> were involved in political and military maneuvering concerning the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech crown</a>, offered by the <a href="/wiki/Hussites" title="Hussites">Hussites</a> first to Jagiełło in 1420. <a href="/wiki/Zbigniew_Ole%C5%9Bnicki_(cardinal)" title="Zbigniew Oleśnicki (cardinal)">Zbigniew Oleśnicki</a> became known as the leading opponent of a union with the Hussite Czech state.<sup>[13]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%22The_death_of_king_Wladyslaw_II_at_Varna%22.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="466" data-file-width="800" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/%22The_death_of_king_Wladyslaw_II_at_Varna%22.jpg/300px-%22The_death_of_king_Wladyslaw_II_at_Varna%22.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/%22The_death_of_king_Wladyslaw_II_at_Varna%22.jpg/450px-%22The_death_of_king_Wladyslaw_II_at_Varna%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/%22The_death_of_king_Wladyslaw_II_at_Varna%22.jpg/600px-%22The_death_of_king_Wladyslaw_II_at_Varna%22.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%22The_death_of_king_Wladyslaw_II_at_Varna%22.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <b><a href="/wiki/Crusade_of_Varna" title="Crusade of Varna">Crusade of Varna</a></b> was a series of events in 1443–44 between the crusaders and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, culminating in a devastating Christian loss at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Varna" title="Battle of Varna">Battle of Varna</a> on 10 November 1444.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Jagiellonian dynasty was not entitled to automatic hereditary succession, as each new king had to be approved by nobility consensus. Władysław Jagiełło had two sons late in life from his last wife, Sophia of Halshany. In 1430 the nobility agreed to the succession of the future <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_III_of_Poland" title="Władysław III of Poland">Władysław III</a>, only after the King gave in and guaranteed the satisfaction of their new demands. In 1434 the old monarch died and his minor son Władysław was crowned; the Royal Council led by Bishop Oleśnicki undertook the regency duties. In 1438 the Czech anti-<a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">Habsburg</a> opposition, mainly Hussite factions, offered the Czech crown to Jagiełło's younger son <a href="/wiki/Casimir_IV_Jagiellon" title="Casimir IV Jagiellon">Casimir IV</a>. The idea, accepted in Poland over Oleśnicki's objections, resulted in two unsuccessful Polish military expeditions to <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a>.<sup>[13]</sup></p>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Vytautas" title="Vytautas">Vytautas</a>' death in 1430 Lithuania became embroiled in internal wars and conflicts with Poland. Casimir IV, sent as a boy by Władysław III on a mission there in 1440, was surprisingly proclaimed by the Lithuanians as a <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duke of Lithuania</a>, and he stayed in Lithuania.<sup>[13]</sup></p>
<p>Oleśnicki gained the upper hand again and pursued his long-term objective of Poland's union with <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>. At that time the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> embarked on a new round of European conquests and threatened Hungary, which needed the powerful Polish–Lithuanian ally. In 1440 Władysław III assumed the Hungarian throne. Influenced by Julian Cesarini, the young king led the Hungarian army against the Ottomans in 1443 and again in 1444. Like Cesarini, Władysław III was killed at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Varna" title="Battle of Varna">Battle of Varna</a>. Beginning toward the end of Jagiełło's life, Poland was practically governed by a magnate oligarchy led by Oleśnicki. The rule of the dignitaries was actively opposed by various <i><a href="/wiki/Szlachta" title="Szlachta">szlachta</a></i> groups. Their leader <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spytek_of_Melsztyn_(died_1399)" title="Spytek of Melsztyn (died 1399)">Spytek of Melsztyn</a> was killed during an <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grotniki" title="Battle of Grotniki">armed confrontation in 1439</a>, which allowed Oleśnicki to purge Poland of the remaining Hussite sympathizers and pursue his other objectives without significant opposition.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Casimir_IV_Jagiellon">Casimir IV Jagiellon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Casimir IV Jagiellon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1445 <a href="/wiki/Casimir_IV_Jagiellon" title="Casimir IV Jagiellon">Casimir</a>, the Grand Duke of Lithuania, was asked to assume the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Polish_monarchs" title="List of Polish monarchs">Polish throne</a> vacated by the death of his brother <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_III_of_Poland" title="Władysław III of Poland">Władysław</a>. Casimir was a tough negotiator and did not accept the Polish nobility's conditions for his election. <a href="/wiki/Casimir_IV_Jagiellon" title="Casimir IV Jagiellon">Casimir Jagiellon</a> was the third and youngest son of King Władysław II Jagiełło and his fourth wife, <a href="/wiki/Sophia_of_Halshany" title="Sophia of Halshany">Sophia of Halshany</a>. His father was already 65 at the time of Casimir’s birth, and his brother Władysław III, three years his senior, was expected to become king before his majority. Strangely, little was done for his education; he was never taught Latin, nor was he trained for the responsibilities of office, despite the fact he was the only brother of the rightful sovereign.<sup>[5]</sup> He often relied on his instinct and feelings and had little political knowledge, but shared a great interest in the diplomacy and economic affairs of the country. Throughout Casimir's youth, Bishop <a href="/wiki/Zbigniew_Ole%C5%9Bnicki_(cardinal)" title="Zbigniew Oleśnicki (cardinal)">Zbigniew Oleśnicki</a> was his mentor and tutor, however, the cleric felt a strong reluctance towards him, believing that he would be an unsuccessful monarch following Władysław's death.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bitwapodchojnicami.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="521" data-file-width="850" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Bitwapodchojnicami.jpg/300px-Bitwapodchojnicami.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Bitwapodchojnicami.jpg/450px-Bitwapodchojnicami.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Bitwapodchojnicami.jpg/600px-Bitwapodchojnicami.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bitwapodchojnicami.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Years%27_War_(1454%E2%80%9366)" title="Thirteen Years' War (1454–66)">Thirteen Years' War</a> - <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chojnice_(1454)" title="Battle of Chojnice (1454)">Battle of Chojnice</a> in 1454</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The sudden death of <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_K%C4%99stutaitis" title="Sigismund Kęstutaitis">Sigismund Kęstutaitis</a> left the office of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a> empty. The Voivode of <a href="/wiki/Trakai" title="Trakai">Trakai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonas_Go%C5%A1tautas" title="Jonas Goštautas">Jonas Goštautas</a>, and other magnates of Lithuania, supported Casimir as a candidate to the throne. However many Polish noblemen hoped that the thirteen-year-old boy would become a Vice-regent for the Polish King in Lithuania. Casimir was invited by the Lithuanian magnates to Lithuania, and when he arrived in <a href="/wiki/Vilnius" title="Vilnius">Vilnius</a> in 1440, he was proclaimed as the Grand Duke of Lithuania on 29 June 1440 by the <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_Council_of_Lords" title="Lithuanian Council of Lords">Council of Lords</a>. Casimir succeeded his brother Władysław III (killed at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Varna" title="Battle of Varna">Battle of Varna</a> in 1444) as King of Poland after a three-year interregnum on 25 June 1447. In 1454, he married <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Austria_(1436%E2%80%931505)" title="Elizabeth of Austria (1436–1505)">Elisabeth of Austria</a>, daughter of the late <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Romans" title="King of the Romans">King of the Romans</a> <a href="/wiki/Albert_II_of_Germany" title="Albert II of Germany">Albert II of Habsburg</a> by his late wife <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Luxembourg" title="Elizabeth of Luxembourg">Elisabeth of Bohemia</a>. Her distant relative <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frederick_of_Habsburg,_King_of_the_Romans" title="Frederick of Habsburg, King of the Romans">Frederick of Habsburg</a> became <a href="/wiki/Frederick_III,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick III, Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> and reigned as <a href="/wiki/Frederick_III,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick III, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick III</a> until after Casimir's own death. The marriage strengthened the ties between the house of Jagiellon and the sovereigns of Hungary-Bohemia and put Casimir at odds with the Holy Roman Emperor through internal Habsburg rivalry. Becoming a King of Poland Casimir also freed himself from the control the <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>n oligarchy had imposed on him; in the Vilnius Privilege of 1447 he declared the Lithuanian nobility having equal rights with Polish <i><a href="/wiki/Szlachta" title="Szlachta">szlachta</a></i>. In time Kazimierz Jagiellończyk was able to remove from power Cardinal Oleśnicki and his group, basing his own power on the younger middle nobility camp instead. A conflict with the pope and the local Church hierarchy over the right to fill vacant bishop positions Casimir also resolved in his favor.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Thirteen_Years.27_War_.281454.E2.80.9366.29">Thirteen Years' War (1454–66)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Thirteen Years' War (1454–66)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>That same year, Casimir was approached by the <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Confederation" title="Prussian Confederation">Prussian Confederation</a> for aid against the <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_Order" title="Teutonic Order">Teutonic Order</a>, which he promised, by making the separatist Prussian regions a protectorate of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Kingdom of Poland">Polish Kingdom</a>. However, when the insurgent cities rebelled against the Order, it resisted and the <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Years%27_War_(1454%E2%80%9366)" title="Thirteen Years' War (1454–66)">Thirteen Years' War</a> (1454–1466) ensued. Casimir and the <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Confederation" title="Prussian Confederation">Prussian Confederation</a> defeated the Teutonic Order, taking over its capital at <a href="/wiki/Malbork" title="Malbork">Marienburg</a> (<a href="/wiki/Malbork_Castle" title="Malbork Castle">Malbork Castle</a>). In the <a href="/wiki/Second_Peace_of_Thorn_(1466)" title="Second Peace of Thorn (1466)">Second Peace of Thorn</a> (1466), the Order recognized Polish sovereignty over the seceded western Prussian regions, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Prussia" title="Royal Prussia">Royal Prussia</a>, and the Polish crown's overlordship over the remaining <a href="/wiki/State_of_the_Teutonic_Order" title="State of the Teutonic Order">Teutonic Monastic State</a>, transformed in 1525 into a duchy, <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Prussia" title="Duchy of Prussia">Ducal Prussia</a>. Poland regained <a href="/wiki/Pomerelia" title="Pomerelia">Pomerelia</a> and with it the all-important access to <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">the Baltic Sea</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Warmia" title="Warmia">Warmia</a>. In addition to land warfare, naval battles had taken place, where ships provided by the <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gdańsk">City of Danzig</a> (Gdańsk) successfully fought <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Danish</a> and Teutonic fleets.<sup>[15]</sup></p>
<p>Other 15th-century Polish territorial gains, or rather revindications, included the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_O%C5%9Bwi%C4%99cim" title="Duchy of Oświęcim">Duchy of Oświęcim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Zator" title="Duchy of Zator">Duchy of Zator</a> on <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a>'s border with <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Poland" title="Lesser Poland">Lesser Poland</a>, and there was notable progress regarding the incorporation of the <a href="/wiki/Masovian_Voivodeship" title="Masovian Voivodeship">Piast Masovian</a> duchies into the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Crown of the Kingdom of Poland">Crown</a>.</p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:527px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Malborkcastle.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="423" data-file-width="1024" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Malborkcastle.jpg/525px-Malborkcastle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Malborkcastle.jpg/788px-Malborkcastle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/31/Malborkcastle.jpg 2x" width="525"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Malborkcastle.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Malbork_Castle" title="Malbork Castle">Malbork Castle</a> during Thirteen Years' War (1460)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkish_and_Tatar_wars">Turkish and Tatar wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Turkish and Tatar wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The influence of the Jagiellonian dynasty in Central Europe had been on the rise. In 1471 Casimir's son <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vladislaus_II_of_Bohemia_and_Hungary" title="Vladislaus II of Bohemia and Hungary">Władysław</a> became a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bohemian_monarchs" title="List of Bohemian monarchs">king of Bohemia</a>, and in 1490 also of <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>. The southern and eastern outskirts of Poland and Lithuania became threatened by <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Turkish</a> invasions beginning in the late 15th century. <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>'s involvement with Poland goes back to 1387, when <a href="/wiki/Petru_I_of_Moldavia" title="Petru I of Moldavia">Petru</a> I, <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Moldavia" title="List of rulers of Moldavia">Hospodar of Moldavia</a>, seeking protection against the Hungarians, paid Jagiełło homage in <a href="/wiki/Lviv" title="Lviv">Lviv</a>, which gave Poland access to the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> ports. In 1485 King Casimir undertook an expedition into Moldavia, after its seaports were overtaken by the Ottoman Turks. The Turkish controlled <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a> raided the eastern territories in 1482 and 1487, until they were confronted by King <a href="/wiki/John_I_Albert" title="John I Albert">Jan Olbracht</a> (John Albert), Casimir's son and successor. Poland was attacked in 1487–1491 by remnants of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>. They had invaded into Poland as far as <a href="/wiki/Lublin" title="Lublin">Lublin</a> before being beaten at Zaslavl. King John Albert in 1497 made an attempt to resolve the Turkish problem militarily, but his efforts were unsuccessful as he was unable to secure effective participation in the war by his brothers, King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ladislaus_III_Jagiellon" title="Ladislaus III Jagiellon">Ladislaus II</a> of Bohemia and Hungary and Alexander, the Grand Duke of Lithuania, and because of the resistance on the part of <a href="/wiki/Stephen_III_of_Moldavia" title="Stephen III of Moldavia">Stephen the Great</a>, the ruler of Moldavia. More Ottoman Empire-instigated destructive Tatar raids took place in 1498, 1499 and 1500. <a href="/wiki/John_I_Albert" title="John I Albert">John Albert</a>'s diplomatic peace efforts that followed were finalized after the king's death in 1503, resulting in a territorial compromise and an unstable truce.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sigismund_I_the_Old_and_Sigismund_II_Augustus">Sigismund I the Old and Sigismund II Augustus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Sigismund I the Old and Sigismund II Augustus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monogrammist_PF_Sigismund_the_Old.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="990" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Monogrammist_PF_Sigismund_the_Old.jpg/170px-Monogrammist_PF_Sigismund_the_Old.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Monogrammist_PF_Sigismund_the_Old.jpg/255px-Monogrammist_PF_Sigismund_the_Old.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Monogrammist_PF_Sigismund_the_Old.jpg/340px-Monogrammist_PF_Sigismund_the_Old.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monogrammist_PF_Sigismund_the_Old.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sigismund_I_the_Old" title="Sigismund I the Old">Sigismund I the Old</a> (1467 –1548), King of Poland and Grand Duke of Lithuania</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Grand Duke <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Jagiellon" title="Alexander Jagiellon">Alexander</a> was elected King of Poland in 1501, after the death of John Albert. In 1506 he was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_I_the_Old" title="Sigismund I the Old">Sigismund I the Old</a> (<i>Zygmunt I Stary</i>) in both Poland and Lithuania, as the political realities were drawing the two states closer together. Prior to that Sigismund had been a <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Silesia" title="Duke of Silesia">Duke of Silesia</a> by the authority of his brother <a href="/wiki/Vladislaus_II_of_Hungary" title="Vladislaus II of Hungary">Ladislaus II of Bohemia</a>, but like other Jagiellon rulers before him, he had not pursued the Polish Crown's claim to Silesia.</p>
<p>After the death of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Jagiellon" title="Alexander Jagiellon">King Alexander I</a>, Sigismund arrived in <a href="/wiki/Vilnius" title="Vilnius">Vilnius</a>, where he was elected by the Lithuanian Ducal Council on 13 September 1506 as Grand Duke of Lithuania, contrary to the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Mielnik" title="Union of Mielnik">Union of Mielnik</a>, which involved a joint Polish-Lithuanian election of a monarch. On 8 December 1506 during the session of the Polish Senate in Piotrków, Sigismund was elected King of Poland. He arrived in Kraków on 20 January 1507 and was crowned four days later in <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Cathedral" title="Wawel Cathedral">Wawel Cathedral</a> by Primate Andrzej Boryszewski. In 1518 Sigismund I married <a href="/wiki/Bona_Sforza" title="Bona Sforza">Bona Sforza d'Aragona</a>, a young, strong-minded Italian princess. Bona's sway over the king and the <a href="/wiki/Magnate" title="Magnate">magnates</a>, her efforts to strengthen the monarch's political position, financial situation, and especially the measures she took to advance her personal and dynastic interests, including the forced royal election of the minor <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_II_Augustus" title="Sigismund II Augustus">Sigismund Augustus</a> in 1529 and his premature coronation in 1530, increased the discontent among <i>szlachta</i> activists.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chicken_War_-_the_rebellion_of_Lw.C3.B3w"><i>Chicken War</i> - the rebellion of Lwów</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Chicken War - the rebellion of Lwów">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rodakowski_Chicken_War.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="590" data-file-width="806" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Rodakowski_Chicken_War.jpg/275px-Rodakowski_Chicken_War.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Rodakowski_Chicken_War.jpg/413px-Rodakowski_Chicken_War.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Rodakowski_Chicken_War.jpg/550px-Rodakowski_Chicken_War.jpg 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rodakowski_Chicken_War.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<b><a href="/wiki/Chicken_War" title="Chicken War">Chicken War</a></b> or <b>Hen War</b>, a 1537 anti-<a href="/wiki/Royalist" title="Royalist">royalis</a>t and anti-absolutist <i>rokosz</i> (rebellion) by the <a href="/wiki/Szlachta" title="Szlachta">Polish nobility</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chicken_War" title="Chicken War">The rebellion of Lwów</a> (the so-called <i>Chicken War</i>) was an anti-royalist and anti-absolutist <i><a href="/wiki/Rokosz" title="Rokosz">rokosz</a></i> (rebellion) by the <a href="/wiki/Szlachta" title="Szlachta">Polish nobility</a> that occurred in 1537. The derisive name was coined by the magnates, who for the most part supported the King and claimed that the "war's" only effect was the near-extinction of the local chickens, eaten by the nobles gathered for the rebellion at Lwów, in <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Poland" title="Lesser Poland">Lesser Poland</a>. The nobility, gathered near the city to meet with a <i><a href="/wiki/Lev%C3%A9e_en_masse" title="Levée en masse">levée en masse</a></i>, called for a military campaign against <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a>. However, the lesser and middle strata of the nobility called a rebellion, or semi-legal rebellion, to force the King to abandon his risky reforms. The nobles presented him with 36 demands, most notably: a cessation of further land acquisitions by <a href="/wiki/Bona_Sforza" title="Bona Sforza">Queen Bona</a>, exemption of the nobility from the tithes, a clean-up of the Treasury rather than its expansion, confirmation and extension of the privileges of the nobility, lifting of the toll or exemption of the nobility from it, adoption of a law concerning <i><a href="/wiki/Incompatibilitas" title="Incompatibilitas">incompatibilitas</a></i> — the incompatibility of certain offices that were not to be joined in the same hand, the carrying out of a law requiring the appointment of only the local nobles to most important local offices and the creation of a body of permanent advisors to the king.<sup>[2]</sup> Finally, the protesters criticised the role of Queen Bona, whom they blamed for the "bad education" of young Prince Sigismund Augustus (the future King Sigismund II Augustus), as well as for seeking to increase her power and influence in the state.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sigismund_II_Augustus">Sigismund II Augustus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sigismund II Augustus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Simmler_Death_of_Barbara_Radziwi%C5%82%C5%82.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="881" data-file-width="1024" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Simmler_Death_of_Barbara_Radziwi%C5%82%C5%82.jpg/275px-Simmler_Death_of_Barbara_Radziwi%C5%82%C5%82.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Simmler_Death_of_Barbara_Radziwi%C5%82%C5%82.jpg/413px-Simmler_Death_of_Barbara_Radziwi%C5%82%C5%82.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Simmler_Death_of_Barbara_Radziwi%C5%82%C5%82.jpg/550px-Simmler_Death_of_Barbara_Radziwi%C5%82%C5%82.jpg 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Simmler_Death_of_Barbara_Radziwi%C5%82%C5%82.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Death of <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Radziwi%C5%82%C5%82" title="Barbara Radziwiłł">Barbara Radziwiłł</a></i> Painting by <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Simmler" title="Józef Simmler">Józef Simmler</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From the outset of his reign, <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_II_Augustus" title="Sigismund II Augustus">Sigismund</a> came into collision with the country's nobility, who had already begun curtailing the power of the great families. The ostensible cause of the nobility's animosity to the King was his second marriage, secretly contracted before his accession to the throne, with (said to be beautiful) Lithuanian Calvinist, <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Radziwi%C5%82%C5%82" title="Barbara Radziwiłł">Barbara Radziwiłł</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Jerzy_Radziwi%C5%82%C5%82" title="Jerzy Radziwiłł">Hetman Jerzy Radziwiłł</a>. Secret marriage was strongly opposed by his mother Bona and by the magnates of the Crown. Sigismund, who took over the reign after his father's death in 1548, overcame the resistance and had Barbara crowned in 1550; a few months later the new queen died. Bona, estranged from her son returned to Italy in 1556, where she died soon afterwards.</p>
<p>Sigismund II possessed to a high degree the tenacity and patience that seem to have characterized all the Jagiellons, and he added to these qualities a dexterity and diplomatic finesse. No other Polish king seems to have so thoroughly understood the nature of the Polish <i><a href="/wiki/Sejm" title="Sejm">sejm</a></i>. Both the Austrian ambassadors and the papal legates testify to the care with which he controlled his nation. Everything went as he wished, they said, because he seemed to know everything in advance. He managed to get more money out of the sejm than his father ever could, and at one of his <i>sejm</i>s he won the hearts of the assembly by unexpectedly appearing before them in the simple grey coat of a <a href="/wiki/Masovian_Voivodeship" title="Masovian Voivodeship">Masovian</a> lord. Like his father, a pro-<a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian</a> by conviction, he contrived even in this respect to carry with him the nation, often distrustful of the Germans. He avoided serious complications with the powerful Turks.</p>
<p>Sigismund II mediated for twenty years between the <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholic Church</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestants</a>. His most striking memorial may have been the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Lublin" title="Union of Lublin">Union of Lublin</a>, which united Poland and Lithuania into the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth</a> — the "<a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Republic of the Two Nations</a>" (Polish:<i>Rzeczpospolita Obojga Narodów</i>, Lithuanian: <i>Abiejų Tautų Respublika</i>). Also, German-speaking <a href="/wiki/Royal_Prussia" title="Royal Prussia">Royal Prussia</a> and Prussian cities were included. This achievement might well have been impossible without Sigismund.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Golden_Age_of_Polish_culture">Golden Age of Polish culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Golden Age of Polish culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WawelZWIEZY.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="412" data-file-width="570" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/WawelZWIEZY.jpg/300px-WawelZWIEZY.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/WawelZWIEZY.jpg/450px-WawelZWIEZY.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b8/WawelZWIEZY.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WawelZWIEZY.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wawel" title="Wawel">Wawel Hill</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Castle" title="Wawel Castle">castle</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Wawel_Cathedral" title="Wawel Cathedral">cathedral</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Polish_Golden_Age" title="Polish Golden Age">Polish "Golden Age"</a>, the period of the reigns of <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_I_the_Old" title="Sigismund I the Old">Sigismund I</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_II_Augustus" title="Sigismund II Augustus">Sigismund II</a>, the last two Jagiellonian kings, or more generally the 16th century, is most often identified with the rise of the culture of <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland" title="Renaissance in Poland">Polish Renaissance</a>. The cultural flowering had its material base in the prosperity of the elites, both the landed nobility and urban patriciate at such centers as <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gdańsk">Gdańsk</a>. As was the case with other European nations, the Renaissance inspiration came in the first place from <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, a process accelerated to some degree by the marriage of Sigismund I to <a href="/wiki/Bona_Sforza" title="Bona Sforza">Bona Sforza</a>. Many Poles traveled to Italy to study and to learn its culture. As imitating Italian ways became very trendy (the royal courts of the two kings provided the leadership and example for everybody else), many Italian artists and thinkers were coming to Poland, some settling and working there for many years. While the pioneering Polish humanists, greatly influenced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Desiderius_Erasmus" title="Desiderius Erasmus">Erasmus of Rotterdam</a>, accomplished the preliminary assimilation of the antiquity culture, the generation that followed was able to put greater emphasis on the development of native elements, and because of its social diversity, advanced the process of national integration. The <a href="/wiki/Jagiellonian_University" title="Jagiellonian University">Academy of Kraków</a> and Sigismund II possessed well-stocked libraries; smaller collections were increasingly common at noble courts, schools and the households of townspeople. Illiteracy levels were falling, as by the end of the 16th century almost every parish ran a school.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Jagiellons_and_the_Habsburgs">The Jagiellons and the Habsburgs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: The Jagiellons and the Habsburgs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1515, during a <a href="/wiki/First_Congress_of_Vienna" title="First Congress of Vienna">congress in Vienna</a>, a dynastic succession arrangement was agreed to between <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor">Maximilian I</a>, Holy Roman Emperor and the Jagiellon brothers, <a href="/wiki/Vladislaus_II_of_Hungary" title="Vladislaus II of Hungary">Vladislaus II of Bohemia</a> and Hungary and Sigismund I of Poland and Lithuania. It was supposed to end the Emperor's support for Poland's enemies, the Teutonic and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Russia" title="History of Russia">Russian states</a>, but after the election of <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a>, Maximilian's successor in 1519, the relations with Sigismund had worsened.<sup>[51]</sup></p>
<p>The Jagiellon rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a> in central Europe was ultimately resolved to the Habsburgs' advantage. The decisive factor that damaged or weakened the monarchies of the last Jagiellons was the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>'s Turkish expansion. Hungary's vulnerability greatly increased after Suleiman the Magnificent took the Belgrade fortress in 1521. To prevent Poland from extending military aid to Hungary, <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman</a> had a Tatar-Turkish force raid southeastern Poland–Lithuania in 1524. The Hungarian army was defeated in 1526 at the Battle of Mohács, where the young <a href="/wiki/Louis_II_of_Hungary" title="Louis II of Hungary">Louis II Jagiellon</a>, son of Vladislas II, was killed. Subsequently, after a period of internal strife and external intervention, Hungary was partitioned between the Habsburgs and the Ottomans.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Hungary_and_Bohemia">Kingdom of Hungary and Bohemia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Hungary and Bohemia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vladislaus_II_of_Hungary">Vladislaus II of Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Vladislaus II of Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="King_of_Bohemia">King of Bohemia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: King of Bohemia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:195px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vladislaus_II_of_Bohemia_and_Hungary.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="583" data-file-width="301" height="374" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Vladislaus_II_of_Bohemia_and_Hungary.jpg/193px-Vladislaus_II_of_Bohemia_and_Hungary.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Vladislaus_II_of_Bohemia_and_Hungary.jpg/289px-Vladislaus_II_of_Bohemia_and_Hungary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6c/Vladislaus_II_of_Bohemia_and_Hungary.jpg 2x" width="193"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vladislaus_II_of_Bohemia_and_Hungary.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<b><a href="/wiki/Vladislaus_II_of_Hungary" title="Vladislaus II of Hungary">Ladislaus II Jagiellon</a></b> (1456 –1516) - King of <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Vladislaus_II_of_Hungary" title="Vladislaus II of Hungary">Vladislaus</a> was born on 1 March 1456, the oldest son of King <a href="/wiki/Casimir_IV_Jagiellon" title="Casimir IV Jagiellon">Casimir IV</a> of Poland and Grand Duke of Lithuania, then the head of the ruling Jagiellon dynasty of Poland, and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Austria_(1436%E2%80%931505)" title="Elizabeth of Austria (1436–1505)">Elizabeth of Austria</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Albert_II_of_Germany" title="Albert II of Germany">Albert</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_German_monarchs" title="List of German monarchs">King of Germany</a>, Hungary and Bohemia. He was christened as the namesake of his grandfather, King <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_II_Jagie%C5%82%C5%82o" title="Władysław II Jagiełło">Władysław Jagiełło</a> of Poland and Lithuania, his maternal uncle King <a href="/wiki/Ladislaus_the_Posthumous" title="Ladislaus the Posthumous">Ladislaus the Posthumous</a> of Bohemia and his paternal uncle <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_III_of_Poland" title="Władysław III of Poland">Władysław III</a> of Poland, an earlier king of Hungary.</p>
<p>He was proposed for the Bohemian throne by the widow of the previous king, <a href="/wiki/George_of_Pod%C4%9Bbrady" title="George of Poděbrady">George of Poděbrady</a>, and was crowned <a href="/wiki/List_of_Bohemian_monarchs" title="List of Bohemian monarchs">King of Bohemia</a> on 22 August 1471. The period after the death of <a href="/wiki/George_of_Pod%C4%9Bbrady" title="George of Poděbrady">George of Poděbrady</a> was a time of conflict for the Bohemian throne (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bohemian_War_(1468%E2%80%931478)" title="Bohemian War (1468–1478)">Bohemian War (1468–1478)</a>), and Vladislaus was unable to confront it. At the time of his arrival in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, he was only fifteen years old and significantly dominated by his advisers. The succession conflict was settled in 1479 in the Peace of Olomouc, which allowed both Vladislaus and <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Corvinus" title="Matthias Corvinus">Matthias Corvinus</a> to use the title "King of Bohemia". Vladislaus would reign in Bohemia proper, while Matthias gained <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">Moravia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a>, and the two Lusatias. The deal also stipulated that in case of Matthias' death, Vladislaus would pay 400,000 gulden for the entirety of the Bohemian lands. However, this payment was not made once Vladislaus became King of Hungary after the death of Matthias.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="King_of_Hungary">King of Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: King of Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Great chaos overcame <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> when the King <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Corvinus" title="Matthias Corvinus">Matthias Corvinus</a> died without heir in 1490. His illegitimate son <a href="/wiki/John_Hunyadi" title="John Hunyadi">John Hunyadi</a> was not recognized by the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_nobility" title="Hungarian nobility">Hungarian nobility</a>, and after being forced to retreat, they called Vladislaus to Hungary, as his mother was the sister of the long ago deceased King Ladislaus and granddaughter of King Sigismund. Vladislaus was then crowned King of Hungary on 18 September 1490.</p>
<p>Vladislaus immediately moved to Hungary, and there he lived the rest of his life, having his court and all his children born in the palace of Buda. The Hungarian nobility reigned and took many important decisions in his name, and his role as monarch soon passed to be in a second plan. <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Z%C3%A1polya" title="Stephen Zápolya">Stephen Zápolya</a>, the archbishop <a href="/wiki/Tam%C3%A1s_Bak%C3%B3cz" title="Tamás Bakócz">Tamás Bakócz</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Szatm%C3%A1ri" title="George Szatmári">George Szatmári</a> continued with the Turkish war plans and tried then to maintain the Kingdom that fell in a severe economical crisis after Matthias's death. Vladislaus was a cheerful man, but after the death of his third wife, he fell into a severe depression and almost retired from all official issues. Then he gained the nickname of "Vladislaus Bene" (Polish: <i>Władysław Dobrze</i>, Hungarian: <i>Dobzse László</i>, Czech: <i>král Dobře</i>) because to almost any request he answered, "Bene" (Latin for "(It is) well").</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Louis_II_of_Hungary">Louis II of Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Louis II of Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lajos_II.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="438" height="276" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Lajos_II.jpg/220px-Lajos_II.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Lajos_II.jpg/330px-Lajos_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0a/Lajos_II.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lajos_II.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<b><a href="/wiki/Louis_II_of_Hungary" title="Louis II of Hungary">Louis II of Hungary</a></b> (1506 - 1526), King of Hungary and Bohemia</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Louis_II_of_Hungary" title="Louis II of Hungary">Louis II</a> was the son of Ladislaus II Jagiellon and his third wife, <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Foix-Candale" title="Anne of Foix-Candale">Anne of Foix-Candale</a>. In 1515 Louis II was married to <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Hungary_(governor_of_the_Netherlands)" title="Mary of Hungary (governor of the Netherlands)">Mary of Austria</a>, granddaughter of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor">Maximilian I</a>, as stipulated by the First Congress of Vienna in 1515. His sister Anne was married to Archduke <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Ferdinand I, Holy Roman Emperor">Ferdinand of Austria</a>, then a governor on behalf of his brother <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a>, and later Emperor Ferdinand I.</p>
<p>Following the accession to the throne of <a href="/wiki/Suleiman_the_Magnificent" title="Suleiman the Magnificent">Suleiman I</a>, the sultan sent an ambassador to <a href="/wiki/Louis_II_of_Hungary" title="Louis II of Hungary">Louis II</a> to collect the annual tribute that Hungary had been subjected to. Louis refused to pay annual tribute and had the Ottoman ambassador executed and sent the head to the Sultan. Louis believed that the Papal States and other Christian States including Charles V, <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> would help him. This event hastened the fall of Hungary. <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">The Ottoman Empire</a> declared war on the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a>, Suleiman postponed his plan to besiege Rhodes and made an expedition to Belgrade. Louis failed to coordinate and gather his forces. At the same time, Hungary was unable to get assistance from other European states, which Louis had hoped for. <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> and many strategic castles in <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> were captured by the Ottomans. This was disastrous for Louis' kingdom; without the strategically important cities of Belgrade and Šabac, Hungary, including Buda, was open to further Turkish conquests.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2lajos.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="702" data-file-width="920" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/2lajos.jpg/275px-2lajos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/2lajos.jpg/413px-2lajos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/2lajos.jpg/550px-2lajos.jpg 2x" width="275"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2lajos.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Discovery of the corpse of King Louis II after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Battle of Mohács">Battle of Mohacs</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Rhodes_(1522)" title="Siege of Rhodes (1522)">siege of Rhodes</a>, in 1526 Suleiman made a second expedition to subdue all of Hungary. Louis made a tactical error when he tried to stop the Ottoman army in an open field battle with a medieval army, insufficient firearms, and obsolete tactics. On 29 August 1526, Louis led his forces against Suleiman the Magnificent of the Ottoman Empire in the disastrous <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Battle of Mohács">Battle of Mohács</a>. In a pincer movement, the Hungarian army was surrounded by Ottoman cavalry, and in the center, the Hungarian heavy knights and infantry were repulsed and suffered heavy casualties, especially from the well-positioned Ottoman cannons and well-armed and trained Janissary musketeers.</p>
<p>Nearly the entire Hungarian Royal army was destroyed on the battlefield. During the retreat, the twenty-year-old king died in a marsh. As Louis had no legitimate children, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Ferdinand I, Holy Roman Emperor">Ferdinand</a> was elected as his successor in the Kingdoms of Bohemia and Hungary, but the Hungarian throne was contested by <a href="/wiki/John_Z%C3%A1polya" title="John Zápolya">John Zápolya</a>, who ruled the areas of the kingdom conquered by the Turks as an Ottoman client.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jagiellons_in_natural_line">Jagiellons in natural line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Jagiellons in natural line">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although Louis II's marriage remained childless, he probably had an illegitimate child with his mother's former lady-in-waiting, <a href="/wiki/Angelitha_Wass" title="Angelitha Wass">Angelitha Wass</a>, before his marriage. This son was called <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1nos_Wass" title="János Wass">John</a> (János in Hungarian). This name appears in sources in Vienna as either János Wass or János Lanthos. The former surname is his mother's maiden name. The latter surname may refer to his occupation. "Lanthos" means "lutenist", or "bard". He received incomes from the Royal Treasury regularly. He had further offspring.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Jagiellonian_Kings_of_Poland">Jagiellonian Kings of Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Jagiellonian Kings of Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td>1530/1548-1572</td>
<td><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elisabeth_of_Austria_(1526-1545)" title="Elisabeth of Austria (1526-1545)">Elisabeth of Austria</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/Barbara_Radziwi%C5%82%C5%82" title="Barbara Radziwiłł">Barbara Radziwiłł</a><br/>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Austria_(1533%E2%80%931572)" title="Catherine of Austria (1533–1572)">Catherine of Austria</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>After Sigismund II Augustus, the dynasty underwent further changes. Sigismund II's heirs were his sisters <a href="/wiki/Anna_Jagiellon" title="Anna Jagiellon">Anna Jagiellon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Jagiellon" title="Catherine Jagiellon">Catherine Jagiellon</a>. The latter had married Duke John of Finland, who thereby from 1569 became King <a href="/wiki/John_III_of_Sweden" title="John III of Sweden">John III of Sweden</a>, and they had a son, <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_III_Vasa" title="Sigismund III Vasa">Sigismund III Vasa</a>; as a result, the Polish branch of the Jagiellonians merged with the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Vasa" title="House of Vasa">House of Vasa</a>, which ruled Poland from 1587 until 1668. During the interval, among others, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_B%C3%A1thory" title="Stephen Báthory">Stephen Báthory</a>, the husband of the childless Anna, reigned.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Jagiellonian_Kings_of_Bohemia.2C_Hungary_and_Croatia">Jagiellonian Kings of Bohemia, Hungary and Croatia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Jagiellonian Kings of Bohemia, Hungary and Croatia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>At one point, the Jagiellonians established dynastic control also over the kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">Bohemia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> (from 1490 onwards), with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vladislaus_II_of_Bohemia_and_Hungary" title="Vladislaus II of Bohemia and Hungary">Vladislaus Jagiello</a> whom several history books call Vladisla(u)s II. After being elected and crowned King of Hungary, Vladislaus moved his court to Hungary from where he ruled both countries and his children were born and raised. By Louis' sudden death in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Battle of Mohács">Battle of Mohács</a> in 1526, that royal line was extinguished in male line.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Krak%C3%B3w" title="University of Kraków">The Jagiellonian University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jagiellonian_Library" title="Jagiellonian Library">Jagiellonian Library</a> of the Jagiellonian University in Kraków</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Globus_Jagellonicus" title="Globus Jagellonicus">Globus Jagellonicus</a>, is by some considered to be the oldest existing globe to show the Americas</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jagiellonian_tapestries" title="Jagiellonian tapestries">Jagiellonian tapestries</a> is a collection of tapestries</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jagiellonia_Bia%C5%82ystok" title="Jagiellonia Białystok">Jagiellonia Białystok</a>, a football club, based in <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82ystok" title="Białystok">Białystok</a></li>
<li>Jagiellonia Tuszyn, a former football club based in <a href="/wiki/Tuszyn" title="Tuszyn">Tuszyn</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jagie%C5%82%C5%82o_Oak" title="Jagiełło Oak">Jagiełło Oak</a>, most noted of the <a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest" title="Białowieża Forest">Białowieża Forest</a> oaks</li>
<li>Jagiellonia, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities_in_North_America" title="Fraternities and sororities in North America">fraternal society</a> founded in 1910 in Vienna</li>
</ul>

<li>Wojciech Dominiak, Bożena Czwojdrak, Beata Jankowiak-Konik, <i>Jagiellonowie</i></li>
<li>Marek Derwich, <i>Monarchia Jagiellonów (1399–1586)</i></li>
<li>Krzysztof Baczkowski, <i>Polska i jej sąsiedzi za Jagiellonów</i></li>
<li>Henryk Litwin, <a class="external text" href="https://www.msz.gov.pl/resource/49da65c5-9917-40de-b542-5c89751cacf6:JCR" rel="nofollow"><i>Central European Superpower</i></a>, <i>BUM Magazine</i>, October 2016.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jagiellonian_dynasty&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Jadwiga was crowned King of Poland — Hedvig Rex Poloniæ, not Hedvig Regina Poloniæ. Polish law had no provision for a female ruler (queen regnant), but did not specify that the King had to be a male. The masculine gender of her title was also meant to emphasize that she was monarch in her own right, not a queen consort.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
